  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

                      <div id="customfield_12310120-val" class="value type-multicheckboxes" data-fieldtype="multicheckboxes" data-fieldtypecompletekey="com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.customfieldtypes:multicheckboxes">

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>The current Maven POM templates only contain dependency information, the bare bones necessary for uploading artifacts to the Maven repository.</p> 
                  <p>The full Maven POMs in the attached patch include the information necessary to run a multi-module Maven build, in addition to serving the same purpose as the current POM templates.</p> 
                  <p>Several dependencies are not available through public maven repositories. A profile in the top-level POM can be activated to install these dependencies from the various <tt>lib/</tt> directories into your local repository. From the top-level directory:</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">mvn -N -Pbootstrap install
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>Once these non-Maven dependencies have been installed, to run all Lucene/Solr tests via Maven's surefire plugin, and populate your local repository with all artifacts, from the top level directory, run:</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">mvn install
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>When one Lucene/Solr module depends on another, the dependency is declared on the <b>artifact(s)</b> produced by the other module and deposited in your local repository, rather than on the other module's un-jarred compiler output in the <tt>build/</tt> directory, so you must run <tt>mvn install</tt> on the other module before its changes are visible to the module that depends on it.</p> 
                  <p>To create all the artifacts without running tests:</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">mvn -DskipTests install
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>I almost always include the <tt>clean</tt> phase when I do a build, e.g.:</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">mvn -DskipTests clean install
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

    How would the BuildListener interface know about dependencies? Does it have some magic way to know this? \\n\\n As an example, lets take modules\\/analysis\\/icu which has 3 dependencies: \\n \\n\\t Lucene core itself (implicit from contrib-build.xml) \\n\\t external dependency: ICU \\n\\t internal dependency: modules\\/analysis\\/common \\n \\n\\n\\n take a look at modules\\/analysis\\/icu\'s pom.xml which has: \\n  \\n   &lt;dependencies&gt;\\n    &lt;dependency&gt;\\n      &lt;groupId&gt;com.ibm.icu&lt;\\/groupId&gt;\\n      &lt;artifactId&gt;icu4j&lt;\\/artifactId&gt;\\n      &lt;version&gt;${icu-version}&lt;\\/version&gt;\\n    &lt;\\/dependency&gt;\\n  &lt;\\/dependencies&gt;\\n \\n  \\n\\n However, our ant builds (that depend on common-build\\/contrib-build) declare their dependencies in a semi-standard way: \\n \\n\\t External dependencies:\\n  \\n &lt;path id=\\\"additional.dependencies\\\"&gt;\\n  &lt;fileset dir=\\\"lib\\\" includes=\\\"icu4j-*.jar\\\"\\/&gt;\\n&lt;\\/path&gt;\\n \\n   \\n\\t Internal dependencies:\\n  \\n &lt;module-uptodate name=\\\"analysis\\/common\\\" \\njarfile=\\\"..\\/build\\/common\\/lucene-analyzers-common-${version}.jar\\\"\\n  property=\\\"analyzers-common.uptodate\\\" classpath.property=\\\"analyzers-common.jar\\\"\\/&gt;\\n \\n   \\n \\n\\n\\n The contrib-build.xml already has a \'dist-maven\' target, that is called recursively. migrate the solr build to extend the lucene build, so everywhere would use it. \\n\\n Furthermore, couldnt we also make a recursive \'test-maven\' target, that generates a maven project to \'download\' or whatever it needs, then tries to run all the tests? \\nIf somehow the maven is broken, the tests simply won\'t pass. \\n\\n I realize that running all of a modules tests again redundantly via \'maven\' might not be the most elegant solution, but it seems like it would test that everything is working.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n You have to invoke compilation from an Ant build in order for this to work. \\n\\n Seems kinda magical to me   \\n\\n The missing part here is figuring out the maven groupId\\/artifactId\\/version, and I  think  this can be dealt with by looking at the manifest in the jar. added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12913350_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Sep\\/10 02:07\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-09-22T02:07:35+0000\'\u003e22\\/Sep\\/10 02:07\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI\'m wondering whether generating poms is just going to make them more mysterious.  While they are templates I can at least see them and they can be validated by XML validators (including IDEs).  Suddenly they are created through a more complex process which we also have to maintain.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAssuming we have well-structured poms in the first place (huge assumption, different issue), are developers unprepared to add the appropriate dependency to the necessary pom? It doesn\'t seem like it\'ll happen very often, most of our artifacts have very few dependencies and we resist increasing them.  We can document the process, make it very clear exactly what needs to be added and where.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAlso, I\'m not sure all jars are going to have the appropriate manifest.  If the pom is generated (like Artifactory can do btw), I\'m not sure it is packaged in the jar?\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI think Robert was onto the right idea with this original proposal: If we consider our modules section and if we add a pom at the modules level and then one for each module, running a build from the modules level will recursively build each module.  If there is something wrong with the poms themselves, maven will fail.  If a dependency is omitted meaning the code cannot be built, maven will fail.  If any of these 2 issues occur, then the build would fail and an issue can be created for those more comfortable with maven to fix.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"cmale\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12913350_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=cmale\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"cmale\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Chris Male\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12913350_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Sep\\/10 02:07\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-09-22T02:07:35+0000\'\u003e22\\/Sep\\/10 02:07\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I\'m wondering whether generating poms is just going to make them more mysterious.  While they are templates I can at least see them and they can be validated by XML validators (including IDEs).  Suddenly they are created through a more complex process which we also have to maintain.   \\n\\n Assuming we have well-structured poms in the first place (huge assumption, different issue), are developers unprepared to add the appropriate dependency to the necessary pom? It doesn\'t seem like it\'ll happen very often, most of our artifacts have very few dependencies and we resist increasing them.  We can document the process, make it very clear exactly what needs to be added and where. \\n\\n Also, I\'m not sure all jars are going to have the appropriate manifest.  If the pom is generated (like Artifactory can do btw), I\'m not sure it is packaged in the jar? \\n\\n I think Robert was onto the right idea with this original proposal: If we consider our modules section and if we add a pom at the modules level and then one for each module, running a build from the modules level will recursively build each module.  If there is something wrong with the poms themselves, maven will fail.  If a dependency is omitted meaning the code cannot be built, maven will fail.  If any of these 2 issues occur, then the build would fail and an issue can be created for those more comfortable with maven to fix.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n of Lucene\\/Solr developers that don\'t want to put in \u003cb\u003eany\u003c\\/b\u003e effort for Maven\'s sake.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eAlso, I\'m not sure all jars Some even have the wrong information in the manifest...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI think we can use .jar digest (SHA-1) as identifiers to look up the appropriate Maven info to automatically set up POM dependencies.  I wrote a script to crawl the central Maven repo for SHA-1 keyed Maven coordinates (groupId:artifactId:version), and it seems to work, but at the rate it\'s progressing, it will take 4 days to finish.  Anyway, it seems like overkill to gather info on all of the ~250k artifacts in the Maven central repo, just to handle the ~80 .jar files in the Lucene\\/Solr source tree.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI found a free service that provides Maven central repo search, including by artifact digest: \u003ca href=\\\"http:\\/\\/www.jarvana.com\\/jarvana\\/search\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttp:\\/\\/www.jarvana.com\\/jarvana\\/search\u003c\\/a\u003e - it uses Lucene to power the search \u003cimg class=\\\"emoticon\\\" src=\\\"\\/jira\\/images\\/icons\\/emoticons\\/smile.png\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" align=\\\"absmiddle\\\" alt=\\\"\\\" border=\\\"0\\\"\\/\u003e.  I plan on using this as the basis for automatic Maven coordinate lookup for arbitrary .jars.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12913361_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=steve_rowe\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Steve Rowe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12913361_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Sep\\/10 02:44\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-09-22T02:44:35+0000\'\u003e22\\/Sep\\/10 02:44\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                     Assuming we have well-structured poms in the first place (huge assumption, different issue), are developers unprepared to add the appropriate dependency to the necessary pom?   \\n\\n If nothing else, it is abundantly clear that there are more than a couple of Lucene\\/Solr developers that don\'t want to put in  any  effort for Maven\'s sake. \\n\\n  Also, I\'m not sure all jars are going to have the appropriate manifest. If the pom is generated (like Artifactory can do btw), I\'m not sure it is packaged in the jar?  \\n\\n I\'ve looked into 10-15 jars, and very few have the required info.  Some even have the wrong information in the manifest... \\n\\n I think we can use .jar digest (SHA-1) as identifiers to look up the appropriate Maven info to automatically set up POM dependencies.  I wrote a script to crawl the central Maven repo for SHA-1 keyed Maven coordinates (groupId:artifactId:version), and it seems to work, but at the rate it\'s progressing, it will take 4 days to finish.  Anyway, it seems like overkill to gather info on all of the ~250k artifacts in the Maven central repo, just to handle the ~80 .jar files in the Lucene\\/Solr source tree.   \\n\\n I found a free service that provides Maven central repo search, including by artifact digest:  http:\\/\\/www.jarvana.com\\/jarvana\\/search  - it uses Lucene to power the search  .  I plan on using this as the basis for automatic Maven coordinate lookup for arbitrary .jars.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12913373\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/LUCENE-2657?focusedCommentId=12913373&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12913373\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"cmale\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12913373_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=cmale\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"cmale\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Chris Male\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - Sure many developers don\'t like maven, but I haven\'t seen any straight out refuse to use it yet (unless I misread the large email thread), they are just demanding ease of use.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eMy concern here is this process is going in the opposite direction by making it vastly more complicated. Sure many developers don\'t like maven, but I haven\'t seen any straight out refuse to use it yet (unless I misread the large email thread), they are just demanding ease of use. \\n\\n My concern here is this process is going in the opposite direction by making it vastly more complicated.  What your proposing sounds like a great app independent of Lucene - a way to convert from an ant build system to a maven one, but I\'m unsure its something that should be part of a build process instead of a once off thing.  Certainly when we are trying to simplify said build process.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12913379\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/LUCENE-2657?focusedCommentId=12913379&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12913379\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12913379_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=steve_rowe\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Steve Rowe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI don\'t see this issue as providing a complete Ant-&gt;Maven conversion system.  The poms I envision will look just like the POM templates after they are interpolated - they will provide Maven coordinates for artifacts and their dependencies, nothing more.  And the process to produce them can be carried out as part of generating Maven artifacts.  I don\'t think they will need to be checked in, but they certainly could be.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIn other words, I don\'t plan on building a complete Maven build configuration here.  Just the bare-bones POMs required to upload artifacts, like the manually synched system we have now.   Only without the manual synching part. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eVive la simplification!\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12913386_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=steve_rowe\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Steve Rowe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12913386_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Sep\\/10 04:24\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-09-22T04:24:51+0000\'\u003e22\\/Sep\\/10 04:24\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I don\'t see this issue as providing a complete Ant-&gt;Maven conversion system.  The poms I envision will look just like the POM templates after they are interpolated - they will provide Maven coordinates for artifacts and their dependencies, nothing more.  And the process to produce them can be carried out as part of generating Maven artifacts.  I don\'t think they will need to be checked in, but they certainly could be. \\n\\n In other words, I don\'t plan on building a complete Maven build configuration here.  Just the bare-bones POMs required to upload artifacts, like the manually synched system we have now.   Only without the manual synching part.  \\n\\n Vive la simplification!              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12913445_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Sep\\/10 07:47\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-09-22T07:47:12+0000\'\u003e22\\/Sep\\/10 07:47\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                     I don\'t see this issue as providing a complete Ant-&gt;Maven conversion system. The poms I envision will look just like the POM templates after they are interpolated - they will provide Maven coordinates for artifacts and their dependencies, nothing more. And the process to produce them can be carried out as part of generating Maven artifacts. I don\'t think they will need to be checked in, but they certainly could be.  \\n\\n Its this sort of middle ground that I\'m unsure about.  We basically have maven support today but not really.  Some people understand how it works, but I\'ve certainly seen users who are dabbling in some development and are confused by our maven support.  I cant think of another project that generates its poms (even ant itself has the poms well-formed inside its codebase) so suddenly our support has become more unusual. \\n\\n What I\'m hoping is that we can actually add quality support for maven in such a way that users wouldn\'t be surprised, developers like you and I can get the benefits we know maven has, and that also simplifies what Robert has to do.   \\n\\n If all we can do at the moment is bolt bits of maven onto ant, I\'m unsure its worth while.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n Is it? \\nWe\'ve avoided that type of thing in the past.  \\n\\n Yes, it constitutes a parallel build process, but the Ant build process would remain the official build.  For example, the artifacts produced by the Maven build will not be exactly the same as those produced by the Ant build process, and so cannot be used as release artifacts. \\n\\n It has been noted elsewhere that a Maven build has never been produced for Lucene.  I hope in this issue to provide that, so that the discussion about whether or not to include it in the source tree has a concrete reference point.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eFirst cut at Maven POMs for Lucene and Solr.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe following script, which installs non-mavenized artifacts into the user\'s local Maven repository, must be run before the Maven build works:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003e mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=com.ibm.icu -DartifactId=icu4j -Dversion=4.4 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=modules\\/analysis\\/icu\\/lib\\/icu4j-4_4.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=xerces -DartifactId=xercesImpl -Dversion=2.9.1-patched-XERCESJ-1257 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=lucene\\/contrib\\/benchmark\\/lib\\/xerces-2.9.1-patched-XERCESJ-1257.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=com.sleepycat -DartifactId=berkeleydb -Dversion=4.7.25 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=lucene\\/contrib\\/db\\/bdb\\/lib\\/db-4.7.25.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=com.sleepycat -DartifactId=berkeleydb-je -Dversion=3.3.93 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=lucene\\/contrib\\/db\\/bdb-je\\/lib\\/je-3.3.93.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=org.apache.solr -DartifactId=solr-commons-csv -Dversion=4.0-SNAPSHOT -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=solr\\/lib\\/commons-csv-1.0-SNAPSHOT-r966014.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=org.apache.solr -DartifactId=solr-noggit -Dversion=r944541 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=solr\\/lib\\/apache-solr-noggit-r944541.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=org.apache.tika -DartifactId=tika-core -Dversion=0.8-SNAPSHOT -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=solr\\/contrib\\/extraction\\/lib\\/tika-core-0.8-SNAPSHOT.jar\\n jar xvf solr\\/contrib\\/extraction\\/lib\\/tika-parsers-0.8-SNAPSHOT.jar META-INF\\/maven\\/org.apache.tika\\/tika-parsers\\/pom.xml\\n mvn install:install-file -Dfile=solr\\/contrib\\/extraction\\/lib\\/tika-parsers-0.8-SNAPSHOT.jar -DpomFile=META-INF\\/maven\\/org.apache.tika\\/tika-parsers\\/pom.xml\\n rm -rf META-INF\\n \u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eEverything compiles (using \u003ctt\u003emvn -DskipTests clean install\u003c\\/tt\u003e).  Except for two Solr tests, all tests pass. The two tests that fail for me (on Win Vista 64, Sun JDK 1.6.0_13) are: JettyWebAppTest and Solr Cell\'s ExtractingRequestHandlerTest.testArabicPDF().\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI have added configurations for running appassembler-maven-plugin (to produce run-time windows and linux scripts with lib\\/ dirs containing dependencies) for all classes with main() functions that are intended as tools rather than static tests.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI haven\'t tried using the POMs as project configuration for IntelliJ, so I\'m not sure how that will go.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis is a work-in-progress.  Please test and let me know if you find problems, or would like to see more stuff added, or if you think the design is all wrong.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOne challenge worth noting is that Maven disallows aggregator POMs (those with a \u003ctt\u003e&lt;modules&gt;\u003c\\/tt\u003e section directing nested Maven invocations) from producing any artifacts other than the POM itself.  As a result, the 4 or 5 locations in the Lucene\\/Solr build that have \\\"mixed content\\\" (to borrow the XML term for mixed nested element and text content) have to be fudged; e.g. the Lucene and Solr core POMs are located in \u003ctt\u003elucene\\/src\\/\u003c\\/tt\u003e and \u003ctt\u003esolr\\/src\\/\u003c\\/tt\u003e, because the aggregator POMs at \u003ctt\u003elucene\\/\u003c\\/tt\u003e and \u003ctt\u003esolr\\/\u003c\\/tt\u003e can\'t produce binary artifacts.  (The conventional Maven way to address this kind of issue is to make the \\\"core\\\" modules be siblings of the nested modules.)\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n title=\'03\\/Oct\\/10 17:04\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-10-03T17:04:57+0000\'\u003e03\\/Oct\\/10 17:04\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    First cut at Maven POMs for Lucene and Solr. \\n\\n The following script, which installs non-mavenized artifacts into the user\'s local Maven repository, must be run before the Maven build works: \\n\\n  \\n  mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=com.ibm.icu -DartifactId=icu4j -Dversion=4.4 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=modules\\/analysis\\/icu\\/lib\\/icu4j-4_4.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=xerces -DartifactId=xercesImpl -Dversion=2.9.1-patched-XERCESJ-1257 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=lucene\\/contrib\\/benchmark\\/lib\\/xerces-2.9.1-patched-XERCESJ-1257.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=com.sleepycat -DartifactId=berkeleydb -Dversion=4.7.25 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=lucene\\/contrib\\/db\\/bdb\\/lib\\/db-4.7.25.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=com.sleepycat -DartifactId=berkeleydb-je -Dversion=3.3.93 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=lucene\\/contrib\\/db\\/bdb-je\\/lib\\/je-3.3.93.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=org.apache.solr -DartifactId=solr-commons-csv -Dversion=4.0-SNAPSHOT -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=solr\\/lib\\/commons-csv-1.0-SNAPSHOT-r966014.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=org.apache.solr -DartifactId=solr-noggit -Dversion=r944541 -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=solr\\/lib\\/apache-solr-noggit-r944541.jar\\n mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=org.apache.tika -DartifactId=tika-core -Dversion=0.8-SNAPSHOT -Dpackaging=jar -Dfile=solr\\/contrib\\/extraction\\/lib\\/tika-core-0.8-SNAPSHOT.jar\\n jar xvf solr\\/contrib\\/extraction\\/lib\\/tika-parsers-0.8-SNAPSHOT.jar META-INF\\/maven\\/org.apache.tika\\/tika-parsers\\/pom.xml\\n mvn install:install-file -Dfile=solr\\/contrib\\/extraction\\/lib\\/tika-parsers-0.8-SNAPSHOT.jar -DpomFile=META-INF\\/maven\\/org.apache.tika\\/tika-parsers\\/pom.xml\\n rm -rf META-INF\\n  \\n  \\n\\n Everything compiles (using  mvn -DskipTests clean install ).  Except for two Solr tests, all tests pass. The two tests that fail for me (on Win Vista 64, Sun JDK 1.6.0_13) are: JettyWebAppTest and Solr Cell\'s ExtractingRequestHandlerTest.testArabicPDF(). \\n\\n I have added configurations for running appassembler-maven-plugin (to produce run-time windows and linux scripts with lib\\/ dirs containing dependencies) for all classes with main() functions that are intended as tools rather than static tests. \\n\\n I haven\'t tried using the POMs as project configuration for IntelliJ, so I\'m not sure how that will go. \\n\\n This is a work-in-progress.  Please test and let me know if you find problems, or would like to see more stuff added, or if you think the design is all wrong. \\n\\n One challenge worth noting is that Maven disallows aggregator POMs (those with a  &lt;modules&gt;  section directing nested Maven invocations) from producing any artifacts other than the POM itself.  As a result, the 4 or 5 locations in the Lucene\\/Solr build that have \\\"mixed content\\\" (to borrow the XML term for mixed nested element and text content) have to be fudged; e.g. the Lucene and Solr core POMs are located in  lucene\\/src\\/  and  solr\\/src\\/ , because the aggregator POMs at  lucene\\/  and  solr\\/  can\'t produce binary artifacts.  (The conventional Maven way to address this kind of issue is to make the \\\"core\\\" modules be siblings of the nested modules.)              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Steve Rowe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12917503_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'04\\/Oct\\/10 07:25\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-10-04T07:25:56+0000\'\u003e04\\/Oct\\/10 07:25\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    This version of the patch puts the third-party non-mavenized .jar installation stuff into a profile in the top-level POM. \\n\\n So instead of running the above-listed script, instead just run the following Maven invocation: \\n  \\n mvn -N -Pbootstrap install\\n \\n  \\n\\n  -N  disables recursive building,  -Pbootstrap  activates the \\\"bootstrap\\\" profile (defined in the POM) and the local repo artifact installation stuff is bound to the \\\"install\\\" phase in the \\\"bootstrap\\\" profile. \\n\\n I discovered that the Tika artifact snapshots (tika-core and tika-parsers) are hosted at the Apache snapshots repository, and that was causing these dependencies not to work properly, so I switched their coordinates to org.apache.solr:solr-tika-*:4.0-SNAPSHOT, so that they will remain stable. \\n\\n Also, the previous patch had some weirdness with the Solr DIH Extras POM - it wasn\'t being treated as a new file, but rather a diff from some other file (the POM template, I think) - anyway, this patch fixes the problem. \\n\\n Everything still compiles, and all tests except the two previously failing tests still pass.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n version of the patch, all tests now pass.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIntelliJ IDEA project import from the Maven configuration mostly works, with the exception that because the Solr core and Solrj modules each include two source directories, and IntelliJ doesn\'t grok this fact from the POMs (specified via \u003ctt\u003ebuild-helper-maven-plugin\u003c\\/tt\u003e configuration), builds including these two modules fail, since they aren\'t seeing all of their source code. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ca href=\\\"http:\\/\\/youtrack.jetbrains.net\\/issue\\/IDEA-27176\\\" projects\\\" button in the maven projects pane - this works for Solr core (\u003ctt\u003ewebapp\\/src\\/\u003c\\/tt\u003e is added a source root), but not for Solrj, likely because the second source root \u003ctt\u003esolr\\/src\\/common\\/\u003c\\/tt\u003e is a sibling of the module root \u003ctt\u003esolr\\/src\\/solrj\\/\u003c\\/tt\u003e, rather than a child.\u003c\\/p\u003e and IntelliJ doesn\'t grok this fact from the POMs (specified via  build-helper-maven-plugin  configuration), builds including these two modules fail, since they aren\'t seeing all of their source code.  \\n\\n  http:\\/\\/youtrack.jetbrains.net\\/issue\\/IDEA-27176  has a work-around for this issue: click on \\\"update folders for all projects\\\" button in the maven projects pane - this works for Solr core ( webapp\\/src\\/  is added a source root), but not for Solrj, likely because the second source root  solr\\/src\\/common\\/  is a sibling of the module root  solr\\/src\\/solrj\\/ , rather than a child.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Steve Rowe - 30\\/Dec\\/10 04:08\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   Changes in this version of the patch: \\n\\n \\n\\t Reduced configuration redundancy: as much as possible, shared configuration is now located in the  lucene-parent  POM. \\n\\t The  solr-aggregator  POM is converted to a  solr-parent  POM, and all Solr modules are now children of it rather than of  lucene-parent .  This POM hosts Solr-specific shared configuration. \\n\\t The solr war is now generated in a new POM located in  solr\\/src\\/webapp\\/ .  This POM also includes an  untested   maven-jetty-plugin  configuration, for use in starting up Solr from Maven, as requested in   SOLR-1218  . \\n\\t A profile in the  lucene-parent  POM to generate source jars for each module:  source-jar . \\n\\t A profile in the  lucene-parent  POM to generate javadoc jars for each module:  javadocs-jar . \\n\\t Consistent MANIFEST.MF entries in all archives, including timestamps generated using embedded Groovy via  gmaven-plugin  and the Subversion revision from  buildhelper-maven-plugin . \\n\\t NOTICE.txt and LICENSE.txt are now placed in META-INF\\/ in all archives \\n\\t The Maven plugin versions are updated to the latest available. \\n \\n\\n\\n All tests pass. \\n\\n If you have used previous versions of the patch, you should re-run  mvn -N -P bootstrap install  from the top level, to install the non-maven dependencies in your local Maven repository.  (Some of the jar names have changed to better reflect their names as used in Solr.) \\n\\n To create binary, javadoc and source jars, and install them in your local repository, run the following at The previous patch attempted to do this from the lucene core and solr core modules, but that solution was deleting their deployed parent POMs, since the reactor build orders the Solr and Lucene parent POMs before the core modules (the parent relationship requires this).\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/ol\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ol\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eLeft to do:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003col\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAdd Ant targets to test the Maven artifacts\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eBackport to branch_3x\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ol\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12982151_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=steve_rowe\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Steve Rowe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - After applying this patch, Maven 2.2.1 (and maybe 3.0.X? - untested) must be installed on your machine in order to run  ant generate-maven-artifacts . \\n\\n Other changes in this patch: \\n\\n \\n\\t Dropped all use of Maven Ant Tasks. \\n\\t The top-level  ant generate-maven-artifacts  now works and is the best way to perform this task, since it will create a single timestamp for all artifacts; this target can also be run from either  solr\\/  or  lucene\\/ . \\n\\t Removed the  generate-maven-artifacts  target from  modules\\/build.xml , and transferred the responsibility for generating  modules\\/*  maven artifacts to  lucene\\/build.xml . \\n\\t The  solr\\/src\\/webapp\\/  module no longer installs or deploys its (empty) sources jar. \\n\\t Remote Maven artifact deployment is no longer included in the Ant build - this can be performed by the Maven build. \\n\\t  mvn clean  no longer removes  solr\\/dist\\/  or  lucene\\/dist\\/ , for two reasons:\\n\\t \\n\\t\\t The Ant build populates  dist\\/  with things that the Maven build should not remove.  Removing just  dist\\/maven\\/  won\'t work, because: \\n\\t\\t I couldn\'t find a nice\\/simple way to remove a directory just once in the reactor build.  The previous patch attempted to do this from the lucene core and solr core modules, but that solution was deleting their deployed parent POMs, since the reactor build orders the Solr and Lucene parent POMs before the core modules (the parent relationship requires this). \\n\\t \\n\\t \\n \\n\\n\\n Left to do: \\n \\n\\t Add Ant targets to test the Maven artifacts \\n\\t Backport to branch_3x \\n     In this patch: \\n\\n \\n\\t  ant generate-maven-artifacts  now works the same as it does on trunk without this patch &#8211; using  maven-ant-tasks  &#8211; except that instead of using the POM I think we should continue to do that. \\n\\n  The only way for maven to survive, is for the users that care about it, to support itself, just like other packaging systems such as debian, redhat rpm, freebsd\\/mac ports, etc etc that we lucene, don\'t deal with.  \\n\\n OK, those are pretty obviously red herrings.  Can we concentrate on the actual issue here without dragging in those extraneous things?  Maven artifacts, not those other things, have been provided by Lucene since the 1.9.1 release.  We obviously  do  deal with Maven. \\n\\n  They can\'t continue to whine to people like me, who don\'t give a shit about it, to support it and produce its crazy ass complicated artifacts.  \\n\\n The latest patch on this release uses the Ant artifacts directly.  POMs are provided.  You know, just like it has been since the 1.9.1 release. \\n\\n  Instead the people who care about these packaging systems, and know how to make them work must deal with them.  \\n\\n Um, like the patch on this issue is doing? \\n\\n  Basically, the ant build system is our build. I think it needs to be able to fully build lucene for a release without involving any other build systems such as Make or Maven.  \\n\\n This patch uses the Ant-produced artifacts to prepare for Maven artifact publishing.  Maven itself is not invoked in the process.  An Ant plugin handles the artifact deployment. \\n\\n I seriously do not understand why this is such a big deal.  Why can\'t we just keep publishing Maven artifacts?  You know, like we have for the past 15-20 releases.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12983130\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/LUCENE-2657?focusedCommentId=12983130&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12983130\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"rcmuir\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12983130_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=rcmuir\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"rcmuir\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Robert Muir\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eHere\'s my suggestion: Let\'s put the stuff in and do a release.  I am pretty sure that we have enough PMC members who want Maven that they can vote on said artifacts w\\/o those who don\'t want Maven to have to bother (even though they are the same artifacts).  Also, Robert, I would specifically ask you, once Steve has done the work, assuming you are the RM, to honestly evaluate whether the production of the artifacts is a burden for you.  If you don\'t want to, then I would suggest you do all the main RM work and you let one of us handle producing the artifacts to be released\\/voted on at the same time.  If it really is a burden, then we can move it to dev-tools or external.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAnd, for the record, there are more than two camps for Maven besides \\\"die maven die\\\" and \\\"maven or die\\\":  I personally think distributing artifacts via the central repository and the explicit requirement to list out dependencies and their versions is a great service and significantly increases uptake of artifacts, but I can live just fine without the day to day crap that is the result of running \\\"mvn XXXX\\\" (where XXXX is not equal to one of the simpler things like compile or test).   Let\'s not be confused about what we are doing when we say we are supporting Maven.  We are just using it to publish artifacts.  The only time that should ever need to be run is during a release (hence it doesn\'t slow down us deciding to do a release, it just slows down, marginally, the actual release process.)  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI totally agree we don\'t want two build systems and I am totally against switching to Maven as a build for all the reasons Robert is (parallel tests, etc.). target, so I instead have \u003ctt\u003egenerate-maven-artifacts\u003c\\/tt\u003e in the child directories explicitly run the \u003ctt\u003eget-maven-poms\u003c\\/tt\u003e target via the As a result, running \u003ctt\u003egenerate-maven-artifacts\u003c\\/tt\u003e from the top level will cause \u003ctt\u003eget-maven-poms\u003c\\/tt\u003e to be run once for each child directory, but the repeated copy operation doesn\'t hurt anything, and the process is quick.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eUnless there are objections, I will commit this tomorrow.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12984108_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=steve_rowe\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Steve Rowe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12984108_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'20\\/Jan\\/11 09:27\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2011-01-20T09:27:53+0000\'\u003e20\\/Jan\\/11 09:27\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Patches implementing my proposal to place the Maven POMs in  dev-tools\\/maven\\/  and add a new top-level Ant target  get-maven-poms , which is invoked by  generate-maven-artifacts .   generate-maven-artifacts  remains in the top-level  build.xml , as well as in  lucene\\/ ,  solr\\/ , and  modules\\/  (trunk only). \\n\\n I couldn\'t figure out a way for  generate-maven-artifacts  under child directories  lucene\\/ ,  solr\\/  and  modules\\/  to depend on the top-level  get-maven-poms  target, so I instead have  generate-maven-artifacts  in the child directories explicitly run the  get-maven-poms  target via the  &lt;ant&gt;  task.  As a result, running  generate-maven-artifacts  from the top level will cause  get-maven-poms  to be run once for each child directory, but the repeated copy operation doesn\'t hurt anything, and the process is quick. \\n\\n Unless there are objections, I will commit this tomorrow.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n The way it\'s set up right now, if you want to use the POMs to drive a build, is that you run \u003ctt\u003eant get-maven-poms\u003c\\/tt\u003e to copy them over to their target locations.
